<Author>vacationloveruk
<Content>A good hotel but no wow factor. Was in Amsterdam for one night with friends. The Marriott had the best price on expedia for a 'five' star. I would classify it four star. Located in central Amsterdam we found the hotel easily, although the lack of a porte coche with a valet was confusing. Eventually somebody took our car from us and we were able to check in. The lobby was small and had no large centre attraction that I like in a hotel. The staff were friendly. The corridors upstairs were confusing and of okay decor. The room was nice, no view but two large beds and a small but clean and elegant bathroom. The TV was pay per view only. Rip off. The concieage was helpfull. I got the impression they get alot of trouble at the hotel. Not long after checking in a man knocked at the door asking if we were using drugs, as the stench of weed on the landing was massive. We were not, but I did think 'when in Rome!'. Also you need a room key to get in the elevator, probably to stop the outcall business that is so popular in this city. We didn't eat in the hotel as the American Hotel over the road had a spectacular dining room, that was much nicer than the Marriot. As it was Xmas it was decorated and felt very festive. As good a place as any to stay, so long as the price is right. From what I saw of the American Hotel I would try and stay there next time.  
<Date>Jan 1, 2009

<Author>azsmitty
<Content>Heart of Amsterdam My family and I (five total with two adults and three kids aged 8, 11 and 12) recently stayed at this Marriott hotel in Amsterdam. It is a first rate Marriott, similar to what you'd find in any big city. The location makes a great jumping off point for exploring the city. You can walk just about anywhere, or take the tram line or water taxi. Although we squeezed five into the smallish four person room, it was no problem.One of the best things about this hotel was that it has a laundry room, and it is free to use it! Our two nights in Amsterdam came in the middle of our two week trip, so the timing was perfect and we were able to get all our clothes washed and dried, although both washer and dryer are small European style and it takes a long time to complete a load.This was one of the only nice hotels we stayed in on our trip (we stayed in BBs and small hotels in all the other cities except for Munich, where we stayed in an equally nice Marriott), but it was perfect and worth the splurge.

<Author>2FK
<Content>Room not warm enough, but location good for sight-seeing There are two parts to this review: the hotel/room 鈥渋n isolation鈥?as itself and then how it fitted in with the weather and locality. So, the hotel itself: yes, good service, decent room, large, comfortable bed (not bad pillows!), relaxing chair to sit in and good if small bathroom with (a pretty good) mixer shower, although the bathroom did lack a heated towel rack. And good location near museums, restaurants and trams. You can walk (quickly) in to Dam square in around half an hour. Characters bar and grill was good 鈥?nice food for what it offered, warm and good for people-watching outside! The one disappointing thing was the lobby which (unlike other Marriots I have been in) was small and you couldn鈥檛 relax in it with a coffee if you wanted to.However, we went between Christmas and New Year and this is why the hotel let itself down badly: firstly, the room was almost constantly only-just-warm-enough, and sometimes cold. Yes, Amsterdam was going through a cold patch (as in just below zero at night) but I would expect a five star hotel to be planned to manage that and cope with it. Instead, the built-in room heating, even when constantly set to 28 degrees, blew out just-about-warm air (although not until after several hours after we initially arrived) and on its own would not have made the room warm enough. When we mentioned this to the Marriot, I was told 鈥渢he hotel is running out of heaters鈥︹€? so clearly it was not just our room. That said, they did bring us an electric heater within 5 minutes and it did help.Another reason I think the room was cold was because it had a nice big window but without double-glazing. Therefore, not only did that mean a lack of warmth but it also provided very poor sound-proofing. We were on the seventh floor but at night we could hear every shout and car door slam in the street below. Yes, the hotel is on a main road but our room faced a side street and at night it was quite noisy on several nights.I do realise that one could argue that we should expect a degree of cold at this time of year, and a degree of noise as it is party season, and that鈥檚 fine if you want to accept that. But one of the reasons we booked a five star hotel was to get a better hotel which should negate those issues. We have stayed in other Marriots before in other cities and at this time of year and they have been fine, but unfortunately this did put us off the chain if we were considering doing another trip next year at this time.Finally, for food, we recommend Het Molenpad at Prinsengracht 653. Excellent food (full meals and snack menu) and great atmosphere.

<Author>Dr_LT
<Content>Ridiculous why this hotel isn't in the top 10. We have stayed in a lot of hotels, some very cheap, some exorbitantly expensive, some very good and some extremely poor. This hotel is one of the very best we have stayed in.We stayed at the Marriot Amsterdam in Dec and booked via the website. I was a bit anxious about booking a standard room as we were traveling with a child and infant. The rate was 189euros with breeakfast which was very good value by European standards.The hotel is well located in the fashion/night district of amsterdam and will take you all of 3 minutes to walk to the center of Liedseplein. The best way to get to the hotel from Schipol is to take the 370 bus from in front of the airport ($3.60euros). This bus stops in front of the American hotel just a stone's throw from the Marriot. Main downside is that the bus comes half hourly on weekdays and only hourly on weekends. Cabs will set you back 35-40euros and the journey takes just as long in peak hour. Another alternative is to catch the train from Schipol into the centraal station and then take the number 5 tram to the hotel (stops also in front of the American hotel).Looks can deceive as the hotel doesnt look impressive from the outside (unlike the American Hotel - which I stayed in October). The service at the reception was very good, friendly and efficient. We found the concierge service to be consistently helpful and friendly.The room we had (252) was amongst the most spacious standard room we have ever had in Europe. Two double sized beds in 1 room with ample space on either side and in between was pretty impressive - much larger than the standard in the American hotel. The bedding was very comfortable and clean. The bathroom was clean and functional with a lot of vanity space around the sink. The shower hose was leaking but was fixed promptly after we filled in a repair slip (all hotels should have one of these) and left it on the door. Internet is not free (8 euros/hr). If tv is important, you'll get a flatscreen tv with a good selection of english channels on cable.Breakfast was adequate with a reasonable selection of continental and American but if you want a classier selection with a lot more ambience, head to the American hotel for this.Overall, a very spacious, clean, functional and friendly hotel in a good location without the bells and whistles. I will come here again with no hesitation.  
<Date>Dec 18, 2008

<Author>CLHughes
<Content>Great Hotel!! Great City!!! Stayed for 2 nights prior to a cruise, and were extremely happy with oor hotel choice. We used our Marriott points for the 2 night stay and were very pleased with our accomodations. Spacious, bright rooms, recently renovated with large, well -lit marble bathrooms. Large flat screen Tv's with many English channels highlighted the rooms many amenities. Irons and ironing boards, robes, and in room safes were available in all room catagories. Upon check-in early in the AM, only 1 of our 3 rooms were ready. No problem, as we used the available room for storing our luggage. Marcel, a concierge/bellman, proved a valuble resource for tourist information. An outstanding employee, patient and eager to help.The hotel location, away from Dam Square and the Central Station proved to be our quiet oasis in a very active city. The canal boat bus stop is located across from the hotel and proved invaluable as a convenient and pleasant means of getting around. After the boats stop service in the evening, a taxi ride from Central Station to the hotel is a flat 20 Euro fee.We did not eat breakfast at the hotel, as it was VERY expensive. We walked across the street to the Satellite Cafe Pancake House located in the Liedesplan and enjoyed a very substantial breakfast for a fraction of the cost. Excellent coffee also.We always try to stay in a Marriott Hotel or one of it's sister brands whenever possible, as the standard of quality always meets our expectations. This Marriott not only met, but exceeded our expectations. Although not the least expensive accomodation in Amsterdam , it is certainly worth it.

<Author>Cweis
<Content>Very comfortable stay My husband and I stayed at the Amsterdam Marriott for 1 night during a stopover en route home from Italy. This was our first visit to Amsterdam.The hotel was a good home base, even though we were only there for a brief stay. We had dinner and then walked over to see the Red Light district - about a 15-20 minute walk. The next morning, we took a canal tour before heading off to the airport. The canal tours conveniently leave from a dock about a 3 minute walk from the hotel. The hotel room itself appeared to have been newly renovated. Very typical and very clean and comfortable.We have gold status with Marriott and so were able to use the executive lounge for happy hour. In addition to drinks, they had both hot and cold appetizers -- and there's a great view of the city from the lounge area.I would definitely stay here again on my next trip to Amsterdam.

<Author>BillyMac4902
<Content>Didn't Live up to our Expectations from a Marriott Hotel We just returned from a two-week European vacation which included stays at other Marriott properties in Athens and Brussels. Our three-night stay in Amsterdam was during the first week of August, 2008The Amsterdam Marriott has an excellent location. As others have said, it is steps away from the tram stop at Leidseplein, one of the central areas of Amsterdam. It is literally two blocks from major attractions such as Vondel Park, Rijks Museum, the Van Gogh Museum and Hard Rock Cafe. The Leidseplein area will provide you with everything you need including outdoor cafes and restaurants, entertainment, shops and stores. From Centraal Station, it is extremely easy to find. Simply, get on the 1,2 or 5 tram and it is about a 10 min ride. If you will be utilizing public transportation for several days, consider buying a Strippen Card from a tobacco shop for 6,90 euros. It will provide you approximately 7 trips on trams or busses. Ordinarily, one ride will cost around 1,30 euro each, so the Strippen Card is a very cost effective way to get around the city. If you have trouble navigating the public transportation or anything in Amsterdam, about 95% of Dutch people speak on average four languages, so you shouldn't have any trouble getting around,Regarding the hotel, I must say first, I am an Elite member of the Marriott Rewards program, and for the past three years have averaged over 100 nights per year at Marriotts. Nothing to be proud of, it simply means I have to travel quite a bit fout of town for my job. However, I remain loyal to the Marriott properties when I travel and have come to expect a certain level of predictibility from the hotel chain. We also utilized award points for these overnight stays, which should not - and did not influence the level of service we received at the Amsterdam Marriott.Check in was smooth and easy, and we were welcomed in the usual way. When we arrived to our room, we found it spacious by European standards, with average sized bathroom and normal ammenities. Yes, the beds are extremely comfortable after a long day of walking and touring.However, I found that the cleanliness of the room was definitely not up to Marriotts standards as the first thing we noticed was residue on the toilet from the previous guest(s). From days on, our room was not cleaned to anyones level of satisfaction. Used glassware was not removed. Glasses were not replaced from our minibar, even a complimentary bathrobe was not refolded and left over the back of a chair. For a full service Marriott, I have never stayed in one that did not provide a complementary telephone call from Guest Services to see if everything was in order, or the lack of turn-down service in the evening.As a Marriott Elite Member, I am offered, and appreciate the complimentary access to the Executive Lounge. While it is an advantage to utilize the breakfast services and evening snacks, we found the lounge had very poor management as there were many underage youngsters utilizing the services sometimes up to midnight - long after the lounge service was closed - to utilize the free internet terminals. While the kids were supposed to be under the guidance of their parents at all times, many parents simply gave them the access cards and left them unsupervised. On several occasions, during normal hours, we wanted to look up tourist activities for the day and had to wait in line for children to complete their activities on Facebook or other internet sites. In short, we found the Executive Lounge very poorly managed.To conclude, you will find the location of this Marriott very convenient. The ammenities are what you should come to expect from the Marriott brand of hotels. However, we found the level of cleanliness from the housekeeping staff, Executive Lounge management and general level of feeling welcomed at this Marriott was sorely lacking. With a modification in the General Management of this Marriott property and their better customer service training, I feel certain your stay will be more special than ours.

<Content>Nice hotel but sketchy city and people We stayed in the Marriot in the city center of Amsterdam for two days. We had never been to Amsterdam but have been to The Netherlands several times. We like the places and people so far but Amsterdam was our least favorite and the Marriot had something to do with that.It was hard to get to from the central train station. We walked for at least 45 minuted before we finally got to the hotel. We arrived at the hotel at 11 am and our room wasn't ready yet. No problem for us because we wanted to explore the city. They offered to hold our luggage so we could go out and about. Everything okay so far.When we returned at 3 PM our room wasn't ready still. Eager to freshen-up we inquired how long it was going to take. 15 minutes the staff said so we opted to wait in the reception area. We ended-up standing around for at least 40 minutes because all the local businessmen seem to use the lounge to keep meetings. No one of the staff offered any drinks or otherwise. When the room was finally ready (after asking at least 6 times) we got a key and that was it. We went up to the room and didn't find our luggage there. We called down to the reception and they appologised for not returning it to us. Then they told us to come down to indentify it but never offered us help to get it to our room! How rude! They didn't even have a cart to use.The room was nice and the hotel itself was great, but the people ruin it. It might be an Amsterdam thing because everyone seemed to be rude. Now don't get me wrong, I'm a New Yorker so I'm used to something. But this was out of the ordinary.The upside is the location of the hotel and the breakfast which is nice. But honestly we won't stay here anymore and we won't visit Amsterdam anymore either. Been there, done that. Never again!

<Author>henryv731_123
<Content>A Good Dependable Stay I stayed two nights at the Amsterdam Marriott in late May and early June. On balance, I was pleased with the hotel and agree with the mostly positive reviews other travelers have offered here. The location is pretty good, especially for the Rijksmuseum (a 5 minute walk) and the Van Gogh museum (a 10 minute walk). The Anne Frank house is about 15 minutes away, and the Red Light District is a little farther, probably around 25 minutes or so.The hotel offers free coffee in the lobby in the morning, which is kind of a nice touch before heading out to start your day.I would add a few additional observations: First, if you're looking for places to eat, the Leidesplein is literally a three minute walk out of the hotel, and it's a place replete with cafes and outdoor seating sure to make you feel like you are having an authentic Amsterdam experience.If you're looking for a quiet table at a canalside cafe, I would also recommend the Jordaan neighborhood. It's in the direction of the Anne Frank house, about a 15 minute walk from the hotel. It's much less crowded than the Leidesplen, and there are a fair number of outdoor table that directly overlook a canal, which is probably the most visible characteristic of Amsterdam.Getting from Central Station to the hotel can be done fairly cheaply on the tram, but if you've got luggage that's at all bulky, I might suggest spending the 20 Euros for a cab.

Pay 鈧?.60 per person to the driver and it will pass up through the town centre, past the flower market on the left (beside a canal) and keep an eye out on your right immeditately past a big busy square (you will have been on the tram about 5 minutes and you will be taking a sharp left turn at this point) for the Marriott in big red letters on the hotel across the road. Get out at the next stop and it is 5 minutes walk or less back. we got ripped of with a taxi who brought us round the city from the station for 20 minutes. <Author>TravellingHoya
<Content>What I've come to expect from a Marriott; Great Location; Helpful Staff I stayed at this Marriott for two nights during a layover between Washington and Delhi with my husband. I have Platinum status with Marriott, so I didn't consider staying anywhere else. I would agree with all of the comments about the outstanding service at this hotel. The concierge helped us out several times by providing great recommendations and perfect directions on how to navigate through town. They also recommended we take a local bus to the airport, instead of a longer route by tram and train or an incredibly expensive taxi.Our room wasn't ready when we arrived, but we were able to relax in the executive lounge while we waited. We ended up with a fantastic room at the front of the hotel and on the top floor. We had a good-sized terrace from where we could enjoy a great view of the canal across the street. The room itself was quite spacious and had all of the amentities you would expect from a Marriott. The US electric plug was wonderful. It was so nice not to have to worry about converters. It was just a little hard to find because it's under a cover, unlike the euro and UK ones.Breakfast was included with the package we booked, which was a great deal because it was 25 euros in the restaurant downstairs. The breakfast buffet was very good. A huge selection of bread, cheese, fruit and hot dishes. We thoroughly enjoyed it, but never would have paid 25 euros for it. Also, internet access in the rooms is incredibly expensive, but fortunately, we were able to use the computers in the executive lounge.The location is great. It's conveniently located to a lot of the sites, but you don't feel like you are in the middle of tourist central. It's just a short walk to the main museums. Across the street there's a large selection of restaurants and bars. And there are bus and tram stops just across the street, that can take you to almost anywhere you need to go. The Holland Casino is also located across the street. It's no Vegas, but it could provide an hour or two of entertainment and admission is free with passes from the hotel.We bought 2-day i amsterdam passes from the airport's tourism desk, which proved a very good value. They were able to answer all sorts of questions for us and they even booked tickets for the next day at the Anne Frank House. The line wasn't too long when we went because it was the end of the day, but I heard that the lines can be quite long during peak times. It's best to book tickets in advance.Back to the Marriott, I think the hotel is able to make up in service what it lacks in charm and character. I'd stay here again, especially if I was traveling on business, as the business services at the hotel seemed great.  
<Date>Apr 27, 2008

<Author>antipodienne
<Content>Extraordinary Service - Seriously Good Enough to Rave About I am not inclined to rave, as my many Trip Advisor reviews will demonstrate. But this hotel was extraordinary and is therefore my first 'five star' rating.Easy stuff to start: The rooms are very large by European standards. I expected a room too small to leave my suitcase open in, and was completely (but happily) mistaken. Very large, comfortable and well appointed rooms appear to be the norm based on my room and those of my colleagues (I saw two others that were the same as mine).Internet connection was speedy, so I think the issues previous reviewers had must have been resolved by the time I visited. It's pricey, but no more so than any other hotel in Europe. In fact cheaper than some.The breakfast buffet is very good with plentiful quantities and options, but I'd suggest going out for lunch and dinner as the hotel's excellent location makes it easy to explore. Now's where I start raving. If service isn't the thing that makes or breaks a stay for you, just skip the rest of this review.Every single staff member at this hotel truly embodies the spirit to serve that the Marriott markets itself on. I've stayed at countless Marriotts and never thought much of it - everyone was OK and the rooms were clean. Other than the Book of Mormon in the bedside table, I can't think of anything that's distinguished Marriott from any other hotel for me in the past. But the people at this hotel put their counterparts - and virtually every other hotel's staff I've ever stayed at - to complete shame.The very busy front desk staff remembered me every time I had cause to pop down (and it's not like I'm particularly distinctive in any way). In fact when I rang on my last day to query something on the bill, the man who answered was the one who'd checked us in several days before and he had remembered both me and the special billing request I'd made. I just about fell over.The most amazing part for me was the concierges, who must attend to literally hundreds of guests each day. Every time we dealt with them I left with great information and a smile on my face. One quick example: Silly me had lost my luggage tags somewhere between my meeting and the hotel and was rushing to pick up my luggage and catch a cab back to the airport. I had to complete a form because I'd lost the tags (which they made quick and painless, even joining me - respectfully - in my own joke about my stupidity to lose my tags), Before I'd even finished signing the form, the second concierge had all of my bags sitting next to me. I hadn't described them or told him anything at all about them - he's just got an extraordinary memory and is very good at his job.Every exchange I had with the hotel staff, even when I was rushing like a mad fool, was not only courteous but also friendly in the very direct Dutch way of being friendly but not obsequious. It was truly a landmark of the stay. And it's the feature that will make me pay extra to stay at the Marriott even when I travel to Amsterdam for leisure. I really have seen evidence of the spirit to serve, rather than reading the beautiful book they put on your nightstand (of the same title) and wondering why I never see those people when I stay at Marriotts around the world. The answer is that they all work in Amsterdam.  
<Date>Mar 23, 2008

<Content>Wonderful Hotel with Updated Rooms! After spending 7 days in Italy where we stayed at somewhat average hotels, arriving at the Marriott in Amsterdam felt incredible. <Author>KKAustin
<Content>Everything you expect from a Marriott First of all let me say that I booked this hotel so I could use my Marriott rewards points and save on the exchange rate. We used the Connexxion airport shuttle that someone else referenced in another review. They were very helpful and efficient. Upon arrival, we were immediately asked if we wanted to upgrade to the club level. For 50 Euro per night I thought it was a little too expensive since you basically get continental breakfast and access to a computer. The room we received was very quiet and clean. We chose a courtyard view to stay away from the street. Rooms are small by US standards but ours was big enough to have one suitcase open and still walk around. Room service was spotty. Although they cleaned every day and changed the sheets when we asked, they left glasses unclean and mirrors not wiped down. We did dine at the Pizza hut restaurant. The food was much better than any US Pizza Hut I ever went to. However, the other room service wasn't very good. The food we received was far undercooked, even though we asked for well done. I had to ask to have it taken off the bill over the phone, as well as when I checked out. The location of this hotel is great. It's within easy walking distance of the museums, the Leidseplein, and a lot of shopping. And, the tram is super easy to catch across the street. My biggest complaint about this hotel is that you get nickel and dimed on everything. Internet is 20 Euro if you want to use it in your room. There's no free wifi and even the business center is expensive. The only inclusive is the free coffee in the lobby if you manage to make it down there before 10am. All in all, if I had the points, I'd stay here again. If I had to pay for it, I'd look elsewhere first. If you plan on booking, you should know that this is a very business centered hotel and you will be charged like a business person. It's safe and nice and will cost you

<Author>FlavieP
<Content>Great for a family break in amsterdam I booked this hotel after reading the reviews on this site and just wanted to share my experiences for all those parents looking for a family friendly hotel in Amsterdam. Having visited Amsterdam in my heady student days I knew it was the kind of city more suited to adult weekend breaks than action packed escapes for kids. Amsterdam is however a great place for a long weekend with young kids if you stay at a hotel like this.Situated on the edge of the museum district and a stones throw from the Vondel Park, this a well located hotel. The tram stops are just opposite the front of the hotel taking you to Centraal Station in less than 10 mins. Museums are in walking distance, as is the famous Liedesplein which is full of bars, restos and 'coffee shops'. Bigger attractions such as Madame Tussauds and the big department stores are a straight tram ride away, again less than 10 mins and very walkable if the weather is fine. The great thing about the hotel is that its in a well lit; safe area well a way from the red light district, something you just don't want your young kids to see. If you are after a charming hotel capturing the spirit of Amsterdam this is not for you. It's an ugly imposing seventies building servicing business travellers and airline crews. The terrible facade however is compenstated by the wonderful views of canal and city. The rooms are very comfortable with fantastic beds, plush decor and smart bathrooms. The daily room service is impeccable and there are nice touches such as turn down service at night (with choccies!) and a daily newspaper. There is also a well stocked bar at reasonable prices. We had a family room which was a bit small for us but okay. There are many connecting rooms so you might be better to go for two small rooms if they aren't too pricey.There are two restaurants. The Bar and Grill serves sanwiches and pizzas to name but few and it's OK. The food is cafe standard and service fine. It's fine with kids as you don't feel under pressure if they start to perform! Price wise its fine too. The Quoy restaurant is more upmarket so we saved this til our last night but it's not riduculous price wise so we could have eaten there more. The kids menu is the same as the bar so not much choice but they will cater to your needs (i.e. no sauce here, cheese on the side not on top etc!! kids!!). Go in early as fills with busniess clients later and you kind of feel that you don't want your kids being noisy while someone is having a business dinner. It is not however a stuffy restaurant and kids are most definately welcomed and catered for. Word of warning: they will serve you kids meals with your main course unless you ask them not to! We waited over an hour for ours. Service is very slow but the food is lovely when it finally gets to your table!Take breakfast if its included as its great. Again its in the Quoy restaurant with a great view of the city rushing by. They will cook you anything and the staff are lovely. They will warm milk and don't care if kids spill things!!Try to get a family package as it includes breakfast (which is too expensive per head otherwise)and kids meals and one of the deluxe refurbished rooms. If you fancy a trip out of Amsterdam go to Majurodam in the Hague. It's Holland in miniature and your kids will love it.All in all, a great hotel if you've got kids as its comfortable, well situated and on the whole, kid friendly.  
<Date>Dec 20, 2007

<Author>Miss_Pie
<Content>Very good location Booked a last minute weekend in Amsterdam so not all hotels were available. This hotel is entirely satisfactory but I could not describe it in the glowing terms that other contributors have done. I had booked it directly on the Marriott website and had requested a non-smoking room. When we arrived at the hotel there were no rooms available so we left our luggage with the concierge and went for a tour of the city. On our return we were allocated a room on the second floor which was a smoking floor. As soon as we stepped out of the lift we could smell the cigarette smoke and the smell in our bedroom was even worse. My husband went down to reception and requested an alternative room. We were then allocated a room on the sixth floor (a non-smoking floor) and this was much better - it is just a pity that we had not been given this room in the first place. The bedroom itself was very comfortable. The people in the room next to us had breakfast in their bedroom and left their dishes outside our room. These dishes lay there all day and were not removed until the evening - not what I would have expected from a hotel of this standard.The breakfast was very good and there was a very large choice at the buffet. The staff in the restaurant were also very pleasant and helpful although the staff on the concierge desk were less helpful.As mentioned in other reviews the situation of the hotel is very good but I think there are probably better hotels in an equally good position.

<Author>Chrssher
<Content>Great for families Spent a weekend here; highly recommend this location for families. We have two boys, ages 6 and 3 and travelling with them in Europe is a challenge at times. Nice amenities, very comfy beds - room in great shape (clean carpets, new wallpaper and bathroom fixtures, etc.) The hotel breakfast is more than abundant - cereals, pastries, eggs (including cooked to order), breakfast meats, yogurt, pancakes (small Dutch ones and cooked to order, along with waffles made to order) as well as assorted cold meats and cheeses. The hotel rate with breakfast included is a steal. The bar and grill has a nicely varied menu, including Pizza Hut pizza (all is available via room service as well, which came in about 20 minutes and was served by a most pleasant gentleman.) Everyone we encountered was more than pleasant, very helpful and friendly and spoke excellent English. The location (just blocks from the Leidseplein, a busy, fun area of restaurants, theaters and shopping) is terrific. You are a short walk from the tram stops, canal boat tours and a casino. A bit longer walk takes you to the Rijksmuseum and Heineken experience. We arrived via train, and had no difficulties taking the trams, even with all of us pulling a suitcase. It was a quick easy trip to the hotel. Would highly recommend this hotel for families - close to trans and sights, with easy connections and lots of restaurant choices (even McDs and BK in close proximity.) It is a nice neighborhood as well; felt very safe here even returning later in the evening.

<Author>Moonette
<Content>Great Hotel! My husband and I stayed at the Amsterdam Marriott one night pre-cruise and used Rewards Points for our stay.Arrival and check-in: We arrived in Amsterdam early and decided to take the train from Schipol Airport to Central Station, and then the #1 tram from CS to the hotel (or a square about 1 block away). The trip was relatively easy and stress-free even though we had to drag 4 pieces of luggage with us. Next time, I think I will use the airport shuttle for a few Euro more.When we got to the hotel around 10:30 am, the front desk was very nice and let us into the room immediately. We were using our points to pay for the night, but they offered us a chance to upgrade to the Executive Level for another 250 Euro, which was the rate had I just booked the room outright. We didn't think we'd eat and/or drink enough to validate spending almost $300 more for a room! ;-) Once nice tough, by the way, was the bowl of mini stroopwafels on the front desk.Our room, on the 6th floor, was average size and spotless. The bed had a wonderful, fluffy matress cover into which you sink. There were also 6 pillows and a great comforter on the bed. When we finally decided to go to bed after a day of seeing Amsterdam, we slept very well in that comfortable bed!The hotel;s location is great! The Marriott is very close to almost anything. While we did buy a Canal Bus pass, we also walked a lot, seeing everything from the flower mart to the RLD on foot. One word of advice if you are walking around Amsterdam: Watch out for the bikes! There are 600,000 bikes in Amsterdam, and it seems like 90% of them are on the roads at any given time. Bicyclists do have the right-of-way, and they don't stop for pedestrians.The one negative comment I have is about the restaurant. . .It's over-priced, and the food was not that good. It wasn't bad, but it definitely wasn't worth the price.We would stay in this hotel again should we make it back to Amsterdam!

<Author>SkiAdcock
<Content>Love the staff at this hotel; great location This is the 10th year I've stayed at this hotel during the annual IBC trade show. The staff is excellent, and the location superb.GETTING TO MARRIOTTThere are 3 ways to get to the AMS Marriott from airport. 1) Taxi. Expensive, but if you have more than 1 person  any type of luggage best way. About 35Euro + tip.2) Connexion hotel shuttle (which I did this trip): 12.50E 1-way; 19.50E RT. You can book at Schipol  they take cc's. Have to call 2-hours prior for return shuttle (or night before). On the return, they tell you up front that the shuttle can be up to 15 minutes late so I booked the timeframe one before I really wanted to get to airport to compensate. The bellstaff has the pick-up schedule at the front desk  will call the shuttle service to arrange pick-up.3) Last is take train from Schipol to Central Station  then backtrack on the 1,2 or 5 Tram to Leidesplain  then a 5-minute walk to hotel. I'm not into schlepping  this trip I always have lots of luggage, so that doesn't work for me but I know others have done it w/ no problem.CHECK-INArrived about 9am. Check-in went easy-peesy. Being Mariott Platinum member, they sent me up to the exec lounge to wait until room was ready. Bellman stored luggage. They're used to that, as they get a lot of morning arrivals.FYI for others. On the credit hold, in addition to the room charges, they put 75Euros (approx $110)/night additional hold on the c.c. EXECUTIVE LOUNGEThe executive lounge is lovely. 2 rooms overlooking the Leidesplain. One room has couches, chairs, tables  2 free internet terminals. The other has a couple of tables/chairs,  is the main section for meals. They have a flatscreen television in one room, and they carry USA Today, Wall Street Journal Europe, and the rest varies - London Times, International Herald Tribune, and an Amsterdam newspaper.Hours:Weekdays: 6am-MidnightWeekend: 6:30am-MidnightBreakfast is served in the lounge:Monday-Friday: 6am-10amSaturday-Sunday: 7am-10amCocktail hours are:Daily: 5:30pm-9:30pmHors d'oeuvres: 5:30pm-7:30pmDessert: 7:30pm-9:30pmWine  beer is free. Hard booze has a charge (form to fill out; honor bar). Wednesday night is the 'manager's reception', and from 6pm-7pm Quoy (the hotel's restaurant) sends up food (lamb, duck, sushi, gourmet type stuff).Brekkie in the morning has dif types of meat, cheeses, 6 dif types of fresh fruit, lots of juices, 8 types of cereal (boxed), hard-boiled eggs, yogurts, toast, pastries, croissants, etc.Cocktail hour munchies vary from Dutch items to seafood to couscous. Also veggie trays and at times cheese trays.Dessert is various desserts (chocolate ones, pastries, cakes, cookies, etc).During the day  until midnight, there's free soda, bottled water, tea  coffee.I LOVE the exec lounge staff here. They're great. Also thumbs up to the guest relations managers. ROOMSThe rooms were recently renovated, and are quite nice. The beds are lovely; you sink into them. 6 pillows. 3 foam; 3 feather. Great duvet. The headboards have nightlights on both sides. Granite sink tops etc. Hairdryer provided, as well as make-up mirror. Usual bathroom amenities. Television gets several channels in multiple languages. CNN is 1  I think Sky is 5. There's a channel called Veronica (channel 16) that has a lot of American television shows (NCIS, The Shield, Profiler, Seinfeld, etc). BBC is on channel 2 or 3. Closet has a lot of hangers, including skirt hangers, and also has a programmable safe that's large enough to hold a laptop. Also has ironing board/iron.The desk has all the outlets built in, and also include 110V US-style outlet too. Note to others. Do not plug your personal hairdryer into the 110V; blows the fuse. I didn't do it, but the electrician mentioned it to me when he repaired the fuse from when the previous occupant did.PHONE/INTERNETThere is for-charge internet access in the rooms  wifi in the lobby. There are also 2 free i-net terminals in the exec lounge, with a limit of 20 minutes at a time. Charge for i-net in room is 19.95E, which includes tax. The sign on the box says noon-noon, but I confirmed w/ guest relations that it's 24-hours from when you log on. Phone charges: 1st 5minutes/each additional minuteLocal Call: .75E/.50ENational: 1.00E/.75EMobile: 2.75E/2.25EUSA/Canada: 3.00E/2.50EEurope: 3.00E/2.50EAsia: 9.00E/8.50EMiddle East/Gulf: 9.00E/8.50ESouth-America: 9.00E/8.50ERussia  Baltic: 9.00E/8.50EAfrica: 9.00E/8.50ESpecial Numbers (0900): 3.50E/3.00EInternet Numbers*: .75E/.50E* starting w/ 0676/0677...Access Fee (0800)*: 2.00E* fixed charged after 60-secondsPlease note that '1-800' numbers ARE NOT TOLL-FREE outside the U.S. and will be charged as international phone calls (3E per number).ROOM SERVICEOpen 24 hours. Rates include tax+service, although there's a line for tip. If they don't deliver in 45 minutes, food is free. HEALTH CLUBHealth club is open 24/7 w/ room key. Treadmills, weights, spa, etc. Nice.If you're more into outdoor stuff, Vondel Park is literally next to the Marriott  you can go running, walking or biking through there. RESTAURANTQuoy is the main restaurant. Have never eaten here, although I've heard good people say good things about it. I've heard the breakfast is pricey so you'd probably want to go elsewhere for brekkie.There's also a Characters bar in the hotel, which is a basic pub bar. Think it has a pool table. And there's a Pizza Hut on site (w/ salad bar). You can charge to room service.CONCIERGE/BELLMANThey're quite helpful. Like other staff, been here quite a long time. They can sell tickets to some (not all) of the museums. I've heard it's good to do that, as it avoids the lines at the museums. Also good for restaurant recommendations etc.LOBBY/GIFTSHOP/BUSINESS CENTER/HOTEL DOCTORThis is the miscellaneous category. The lobby is ok. Not super large or exotic, but servicable. Same as the exterior of the hotel. There is a gift shop w/ most of the usual stuff, plus AMS type gift items which I've purchased in the past. There is a biz center w/ the usual stuff. Boarding pass printing is free, btw. Charge for other stuff.Each elevator foyer has a plate w/ apples for guests. Elevators require a room key to operate.Had a bit of a medical problem during my stay. Nothing urgent, but needed antibiotics which requires a prescription. US doctor can't prescribe over here, so needed to use local doc. Hotel had on-call doc call me in my room, and then I went over to doc's office ('bout 10 minutes away). Because I went there for quick test, rate was 20E cash vs 100E if doc came to hotel room. Got prescription  had it filled at pharmacy around the corner hotel recommended (12.11E for 'script). STAFFI can't speak highly enough of the guest relations managers  the executive lounge staff, not to mention the GM of the hotel!!! They're all excellent  truly kept track of things/were so service friendly, I rank them as some of the tops in the Marriott chain.LOCATIONI like the location of the Marriott. It overlooks the Leidesplain, and is only a few minutes away from Museumplein  a lot of other attractions. Doesn't really take long to get to any attractions. Nice central location. Also, there's a canal close to it so people can sign up for canal tours there, etc.

<Author>emmi331
<Content>I Was Grateful for the Marriott! On my last few days in Europe, I decided to splurge and stay at the Marriott. When I checked in, I was assigned a room that connected to another and I could immediately hear the conversations and television in the next room through the connecting door. I asked to be assigned to another room, and the young woman at the desk cheerfully complied, apologizing for not checking with me first to see if a connecting room was okay. I was moved to a very nice room overlooking the square. This room was generously sized, with two double beds (the mattresses were a bit soft for me, but comfortable enough), and an immaculate, well-appointed bathroom.Unhappily, the second morning I was in Amsterdam I suffered a back spasm, and was in serious pain. Thank heavens for the kind concierge, who put me in touch with an excellent doctor and made sure I knew when and where my prescriptions were ready.I was able to get around a bit after that to see the sights, but it was wonderful to return to a comfortable and attractive hotel room to rest when needed.One drawback (aside from the stratospheric prices in the restaurant) was not having a coffeemaker in the room. Fresh coffee was available each morning in the lobby, however - incredibly, for free.The convenient location, sense of luxurious comfort, and courteous service (especially at a time when I really needed it) made the Amsterdam Marriott a hotel I would recommend to one and all.

<Author>WalterWalter
<Content>Mouse in hotel restaurant My wife and me had booked this hotel for our twentieth wedding anniverasry. We browsed several hotel sites on the web before deciding on the Marriott Amsterdam. As is the norm on most hotel sites you are given the impression of grand lobbies and facades only to find a lobby that is slightly larger than a normal house kitchen.Our room was not so bad, with a view of the square in front of the hotel. The only thing that bothered us was a smell that constantly was coming from the bathroom.We decided to eat at the Quoy restaurant which is the main restaurant at this hotel. As soon as we started eating I noticed a mouse crossing the restaurant floor and entering one of the cupboards that are used for cutlery and napkins. I immediatly went to talk to the waitress who seemed to imply that it is normal.We have travelled to many countries and eaten in many restaurants, but have never seen a mouse in a restaurant.We talked to the hotel manager and advised her that we will not be eating any food from this hotel, not even the breakfast which was pre-paid.What was strange was the fact that the restaurant was kept open as if nothing had happened. Mice mean disease and uncleanliness.To add insult to injury on check-out they didnt deduct the costs of the breakfasts that we hadnt eaten from there.I have waited for 3 months for a response from the hotel management before writing this report as they know very well how distressed my wife was because of the mouse.In fact we are members of the Marriott Rewards scheme and I can inform them from here that I will be sending back my membership in disgust.W. <Author>abcdefghi
<Content>No soundproofing Amsterdam Marriott Hotel is a recently renovated 5 star hotel by Leidseplein. It's close to the Rijksmuseum, the Van Gogh Museum and right by a canal boat stop. Several trams stop right by, making it easy to get around the city. I recommend crossing the canal to have champagne breakfast at the famous Caf茅 Americain.We stayed at this hotel for three days. We were given a room on the 10th floor, and it was well equipped and had a very comfortable king bed. The bathroom was quite small, and the toiletries were limited to basics (but they smelled great - lemongrass, I believe). The room could have been cleaned better; - there were greasy fingerprints on the inside of the window and the carpet was very thick and apparently difficult to vacuum properly. We would, however, have been quite pleased with the room had it not been for the noise. There was a machine-like sound that made it impossible to fall asleep (it felt like being aboard a ferry). After a night without any sleep, we complained, and were told that they would look into it. We got back to our room to find that they had placed a piece of cardboard over the bathroom fan (which is impossible to switch off at night). However, the next night proved that the bathroom fan had not been the culprit. The noise was still there, and it was not coming from the bathroom, but from somewhere outside the room. After another night without any sleep, we asked for a new room. When we returned to the hotel that night, they had moved our suitcases to the new room. It was on the 6th floor, close by the elevator, facing the street, and it was smaller and not as well appointed as the room we had been in. Hint to the hotel: When someone complaines and shows great patience by letting you try to resolve the situation first, and you're not able to, which results in guests that haven't slept properly for two nights, and you have to move them, at least have the decency to give them a room of equal or better standard. The new room had a harder, less comfortable bed, only one nightstand (which translates to one nightstand lamp without blue light; not good news if you like to read), fewer toiletries (no conditioner for instance), no bathrobe, and a more limited minibar selection. Housekeeping seemed to have the same problem vacuuming the carpet in this room, and the bathroom fan could not be switched off here either. Fortunately, though, there wasn't the same machine-like sound to keep us awake at night. But who needs machine-like sounds to keep you awake at night when the room isn't soundproofed? We heard every word of the conversations in the rooms next to us, we heard the people in the hallway, not to mention the traffic outside, and we woke up every time an ambulance passed by.When cheking out, the receptionist asked us if we had any suggestions for them on how they could improve, and I said that they ought to work on the noise problem. She answered me back saying yes, well, it's a busy city. Second hint to the hotel: I know very well that Amsterdam is a busy city, and apparently so do you. That is the reason why you should install proper soundproofing. People expect that from a 5 star hotel.I should also mention that there is internet access in the rooms, but it's very expensive (I think it was 鈧?0 per day). I always find it tacky when five star hotels charge extra for internet access, I really think it should be free.If you're going to stay at this hotel, I suggest asking for one of their larger rooms not facing the street, and keep your fingers crossed that you don't wind up in the room with the machine-like noise.

<Author>njtravelpros
<Content>Just Back from Amsterdam Marriott My husband and I have just returned from our 8 night stay at the Marriott Hotel in Amsterdam. Our flight from the USA arrrived into AMS at 6:30AM and after quickly going through customs and avoiding baggage claim since we do carry-on whenever possible, we headed downstairs and took the train to Central Station and then the #2 tram which lets you off a short walk from the hotel. (You can take the 1, 2 or 5 tram to the hotel from the Central Station) All in all an effortless trip and very inexpensive (approximately $8 per person).Upon our arrival at the hotel we were told our room was not ready, which we had expected since it was 8:00 in the morning. We were directed to the 9th floor Executive Lounge since my husband is a Platinum Marriott member. What a great perk to have use of this lounge..........a great breakfast every morning, afternoon snacks and cocktails and evening coffee, tea and deserts. Also, located in the lounge are 2 computers with high speed internet connections available for use at no charge (in room internet costs 20 Euro per day).The hotel is very well run. The staff is very polite and everyone that we encountered spoke excellent English. The newly renovated rooms are excellent, large enough, and the bathrooms well appointed and very modern with brand new fixtures. The location of the hotel is excellent due to the close proximity and an easy walk to the major museums, abundant shopping areas and varied restaurant choices. We had a rental car for 3 days and utilized the hotel parking, no problem, although at 30 Euros per day a bit expensive.As far as the hotel, I can say not a negative word about the facility or the staff. As previous reviews have mentioned, the outside appearance of the hotel might lead one to have less than great expectations. But once inside everything is terrific! We would not hesitate to stay here again while in Amsterdam.

<Content>Great Location! I recently spent two nights at the Amsterdam Marriott with my teenagers. We used Marriott points for one room on a regular floor. <Author>mkent924
<Content>No need to look further There simply is no need to look further for a comfortable, spacious, friendly, and ideally situated hotel in Amsterdam. We stayed for four nights at this hotel from Aug. 2-6. It is ideally located across from the square in Leidseplein, adjacent to Vondel Park, with a canal tour boat access across the street. The hotel has larger rooms than the American Hotel located across the street, and even offers an American outlet for any U.S. appliance you saw fit to haul across the ocean. The staff goes out of their way to be friendly and accomodating, and the Concierge staff is most helpful for anything you wish to accomplish from museum ticket purchases to obtaining a taxi to the Airport at your appointed time. The room quality is excellent, and my wife and daughter felt right at home. It is a few short blocks to walk to the Rijksmuseum and Van Gogh Museum. There is even a Pizza Hut inside the hotel, and if you venture outside, directly across the street, you will find an authentic Dutch Pancake house which is not a bad stop for breakfast. This is an ideal family hotel if you want to go to Amsterdam, and want to avoid hotels in areas adjacent to the more adult oriented sights Amsterdam has to offer. This hotel will get a return visit-no question about it.

<Author>CoClare
<Content>nice stay Finding a good hotel room for four (2 adults  2 children) in Europe is never easy. Our room at the Marriott Amsterdam was good size (by European standards), and the toilet/shower area was separate from the sink. We had a balcony overlooking the little park and canal, and had access to the Executive Lounge which was a great place to pick up coffee and fruit. The staff was friendly and helpful, the location suitable for walking to museums or taking the tram, and the hotel was clean and quiet. Amsterdam is a accommodating town for families, as long as you don't do anything silly regarding the more notorious (though overplayed) areas. Be aware that there are virtually no taxi stands, but anyplace will call one for you if needed. And don't worry, their English is vastly better than our Dutch. We would recommend both the city and this hotel.

<Author>kwh
<Content>Convenient Location The hotel is situated near the Leidseplein, which is a very crowded square, but it is on the other side of the canal, so it is also separated from the Leidseplein madness. We had a clean, quiet room. There are also rooms with nice views of the Leidseplein, but the woman at the desk said they could be rather noisy. The hotel is very convenient for the art museums, and you can catch a tram just outside the hotel that will take you just about everywhere in the city. The hotel is close enough to everything, but far enough outside of the central section of the city to provide an escape from Amsterdam's hectic atmosphere. In regard to atmosphere, the hotel is rather generic Marriott American, and it doesn't offer European charm. So if you want that or if you want to be close to the train station, you probably should look elsewhere, but we found our experience here very positive.

<Author>moobaby214
<Content>Great Hotel and Location! We arrived late afternoon with two rooms booked. I decided to pay vs using points. Both rooms were on the 10th floor on the executive levels. The renovation is done and the rooms are nice. Big flat screen TV, good lights, nice desk and a very modern bathroom. The lounge is on the 9th floor and gets very busy. Breakfast is good open 6am to 10am weekdays and 7am to 10am weekends. Cocktails hour is from 530pm to 930pm with food served. They have two computers in the lounge for free. Overall a good lounge with great finger food at night. The gym open 24 hours is not bad for a hotel. They have 10 or so lifestyle tread mills/bikes. A full free weight area with at least 10 workout machines. One large rack in the middle of the floor. They offer water and towels plus a locker room. I used the gym everyday and was never super busy. The location of the Marriott is very good. As with any hotel in Amsterdam, walking to anything is not that far. What I liked is it was quite. Our rooms faced the backside of the hotel not a sound could be heard. They do have rooms that face the main street. I would not want one of those. Not saying it would be bad but why take the chance. Ask for a room not facing the street. We walked the city 3 times from the Marriott it was easy. Overall I am very happy with our choice of the Marriott. While it is rather expensive you get what you pay for. We did eat here once and the food was excellent. No complaints here at all!

<Author>Robinhoodguy
<Content>civilized city accomodation we stayed at the amsterdam marriot a week ago. after having previously visited amsterdam and stayed at lovely quiet hotels out of town this time we needed to be in the centre due to some temporary mobility problems.the hotel didnt dissapoint; the rooms are beautiful and the beds simply amazing. i wish i new what they were, i'd buy one, we had two fantastic nights sleep in a huge king size.we had an incredible view of amsterdam, and the room was cool and airy. the only dissapointment i have is that there are no facilities to make tea or coffee in the room. We had upgraded to the executive lounge so could go and fetch whatever we wanted but it would be nice to not have to leave the room early in the morning for a tea or coffee. only a minor thing though. the executive lounge may not be amazing value for what you get in terms of food, but simply having a pleasant place to relax, get a drink and a cookie, maybe surf the internet and print off information for your next days activities was really useful and welcome. the breakfast buffet itself is fairly standard continental fayre, and i rather enjoyed the relaxed informal atmosphere in the room at breakfast time, people often share tables and it all seems a little friendlier than sitting just in rigid ones or twos.the staff were friendly and courteous, even the lady i almost floored swinging my bag back onto my shoulder in the corridor as we arrived! the concierge service was helpful in my request for sporting event tickets, though i did get 2 different answers from the 2 guys i asked over 2 days, i still got what i needed. the hotel doesnt feel oppresively posh; it has some pretty relaxed public areas, the bar actually looks like a bar and there's a place to grab a Kip sate and frites or a pizza as well as a more formal restaurant. (the pizzas looked very small though) while we were in reception we heard a bride from the UK complain that her room was filthy and demanding her money back but that wasnt our experience. i guess mistakes happen; or maybe some people just over react. after we left we spent a week in a cottage in rural holland with the family. but both of us wished we were heading back to the marriot for a few more nights before we returned home.

<Author>name_screen

<Content>Refurbished rooms are outstanding!!!! I recently stayed at this hotel through priceline for a very reasonable $110 and came away very impressed. If you read through the past reviews, the consensus is that the hotel, while in a great location near the Museums and Vondelpark, left a little to be desired. Recently the hotel went through some rather major renovations and this probably contributed greatly to the bargain price. Anyway, I cannot say enough about the quality of the newly renovated room I stayed in. You can get a good idea of the value management placed on imparting a luxurious impression to the visitor by the quality of the improvements. Lets start with a 42 inch high definition flat screen television. How is that for luxury. In the bathroom we have black granite countertops, Grohe faucets, Villeroy and Bosch sink, and real porcelain tub. Then we move on to what looks to be solid cherry wood accents throughout. In the bedroom we have a nice Marriott take on Sheratons Heavenly bed. Very cushy, plenty of pillows, etc.... The desktop is solid black granite, with a nice high end leather or leather look chair. The rug was a beautiful red pattern somewhat akin to a Belgian rug. You get the picture. This is serious luxury we are talking here. The room itself, and the outside matching renovated hallway look 5 star all the way. The other parts of the hotel. Well, they were not bad. The outside of the hotel is not renovated and appears seriously dated.Inside the lobby, the renovations are not as obvious. Although the area does look new, it does not stand out. The location of the hotel is quite ideal. Walking out the door straight ahead about two blocks you head straight into the center of one of the cities hottest Restaurant sections (Leidesplein). and a Tram stop for convenient transport to the Central Station area. You can of course walk to Central station from the Marriott, but it is quite a nice hike. I would say 40 minutes or so. Also a short walk accross the street are a number of Canal tours. To the right one block or so is one of the cities largest parks (Vondelpark), another block or so down is the Rijksmuseum where you can see many of Rembrandts finest works. The Van Gogh museum is also in this area.  I tried the Quo restaurant for the breakfast buffet at $25 Euros and was underwhelmed at the quality of the offerings at that price. A few days later, for comparison, I tried the breakfast buffet at the American Hotel and formed a similar impression. This time it was only $21 Euros. Anyway, you get the picture. If you can get this hotel at the price I paid via Priceline you will likely get yourself a luxurious room at a great location for sightseeing.

<Content>Excellent location - Executive Level worth it. We stayed here for one night after having been in Amsterdam, Brussels and Cologne for the last week. We had reserved a free room through a frequent traveler program and were asked on check-in if we wanted to pay 50 Euro for an upgrade to the Executive Level. The upgrade would include an happy hour appetizer reception in the evening, breakfast in the morning, internet access and an upgraded room. We went for it and were glad we did.I've stayed in this hotel several times before and knew that the location was very convenient but I had never stayed in a room as large as the one we got as a result of the upgrade. It was huge and looked out at the Leidensplein. The happy hour was quite nice and the appetizers were good. The place was busy but not overly crowded. The bed was extremely comfortable and we had no problems sleeping even though the area is very busy and can be very noisy at night. The breakfast was good, not spectacular. Even so we had our fill. The internet stations in the executive lounge were useful and a printer was available.

<Author>Bank-r
<Content>Very nice Our group (4 couples mid-thirties) stayed in the Marriott for 2 nights (May 11-13). We booked directly with Marriott and had no problems whatsoever. Price was a little bit high at 160 eur per night with no breakfast, but we enjoyed the experience. All 4 rooms were spotless, bathroom was small but very nice and everything lookedreally new. I normally try to travel to Four Seasons, and the Marriott, though not luxurious, was perfectly fine.My only complain would be that the mattress was too soft and with a duvet cover that made it even softer. I felt it on my back the day after, as I'm used to a harder mattress. We weren't cold though with a duvet under and a duvet on top. I recommend buying the tickets to the museums at the concierge. We didn't do it for the Rijksmuseum and had to wait in line for about 25 min. We learned form it and bought them the day after before goingto the Van Gogh museum. Both cost 10eur and both are worth a visit. We also took a 75min touristic cruise through the canals with the company recommended by the concierge (also 10eur). It was fine, though not spectacular.We used Schiphol Travel Taxi to get to the hotel from the airport. It was a lot cheaper as we were a group of 8 people. They made us wait for about half an hour in the airport, but got us to the hotel really fast. You can also take the train to centraal station for 3.5eur and then take trams 1, 2 or 5 to Leidsplein 1.60 eur per way.Leidsplein has many bars and restaurants. It's right next to the hotel, but it's far enough so you don't hear the noise. When we go back to Amsterdam we will defenetely try the Marriott again. Perfect location next to the Museums, next to Leidsplein and only 15-20 min walking to Dam square or centraal station.

<Author>Michael from Vienna
<Content>Good Hotel, great location We stayed for the second time at the amsterdam Marriott for the weekend April 29/May 1.The rooms renovation program was finished by now and the rooms really met all of our expectations. Beds are very comfortable, air condition working properly and bathrooms are small but very elegant.We asked for a non-smoking room and two beds on a high floor ans all wished became fulfilled.Rooms to the front of the hotel have huge windows but traffic noise can be heard, even when windows are closed. Since we love the view, this does not affect us, but if you want to have a silent room, ask for courtyard or side street view.We did not have breakfast in the hotel, since its quite expensive and there are plenty of charming Cafes around. we also did not use internet this time since we thought it was overpaid.There is a Grill restaurant and a Pizza Hut in the Hotel, but we only had coffee there.The staff is helpful and friendly, there is even a small souvenir shop in the Lobby for those not wanting to look around for souvenirs.Our personal Hotel recommendations:Ask for two beds since those rooms are bigger the ones with one double bed, if you like a nice view, ask for front side but high floor (but be aware, that street can be heard).Avoid breakfast if its not included in the rate and avoid internet, look for internet cafes around, there are plenty !!Recommendations for Amsterdam:You have to make a Canal tour, there is a company right across the square, if you leave the hotel to your right, opposite the Casino.Go to see the red light district, but take care, no photos of the girls in the windows. There are guys around to avoid this.Just take good shoes and walk along the little canals early morning, such charming views.The hotel is renting bikes for 10 Euro per day, reserve the day before because they only have a limited number. Drive around early moning and go to Vodel Park next to the hotel, very peaceful dont worry the traffic, they take care on bikers, since biking is very common in Holland.We will for sure stay again at the Marriott.

<Author>4vrongo
<Content>renovated rooms lovely but make sure yours has heat We stayed at the Marriot on March 20-23 with our two young adults and our past exchange student from Spain. The location is great for families with teenagers or young adults as it is a very safe but active place for them to be. They went out at night without us and we felt very secure about it.  The hotel renovations are still going on as reported and for us the first day started noise at 8:30 the next at 7 am. We had booked two executive rooms that were on two separate floors 3 and 7th because the executive floor is not finished however both were renovated rooms which are lovely. Only problem our second room with our kids did not have heat. Totally renovated with all the thermostats but no vent. At 1 am when our kids called down they at first said just turn on the thermostat then after complaints sent someone up who noticed no vent. They then sent a portable heater. At 330 euro's a night this was kind of overpriced for not having heat when it was only a high of 39 during the day. We were very happy though with the friendliness of the staff and really our only problem was the heat. In the excecutive lounge which is located temporarily next to the meeting rooms they do take down breakfast at 10am so if you are on vacation with young people you have to be prompt.I think once all the renovations are complete it will be an excellent hotel to stay at.

<Author>SpottedCat
<Content>Great hotel, very expensive We stayed at this property on March 13, 2007 after deciding to stay another night in Amsterdam. We had previously stayed at the Hotel Vondel, and it was booked for that evening. The Mariott was a very nice property, however, fairly expensive. We were out and about the city most of the evening, so we spent little time in the room. The bed was very comfortable and the bathroom updated and clean. We got a great night's sleep here (probably the best while in Europe). The concierge was helpful in calling us a cab to Schipol in the morning. We needed more Euros and used the hotels cash exchange service with a credit card. I do not recommend this, as we were charged a high fee and got a low exchange for our dollar. Overall, I would spend the money on this hotel only if you plan to spend a great deal of time in the room. The Hotel Vondel was a better quality and a much more reasonable rate.

<Author>LizzieAn
<Content>New Year In Amsterdam Visited Amsterdam and stayed at the Marriott for 5 days over the New Year period The location of the hotel is great, close to museums (Rijksmuseum, Van Gogh Museum, ) and a short walk to the Leidseplein with many restaurants  bars. It is right beside the canal bus stop and a canal boat trip. It's also close to the shopping on PC Hoofstraat.Check-in was very easy and friendly, and the concierge was extremely knowledgeable. And we would recommend the Aran Irish Pub for breakfastOur room was on the front of the hotel and was large and comfortable - the bathroom looked a bit tired but was perfectly adequate. Not all rooms have been upgraded as yet as the hotel is going thorugh a refurbishment programme. The room had a view of Leidesplein which was great for celebrating New Year ( as it was raining !) !Overall a good hotel and will be great when the refurbishment is complete - but don't let that put you off right now. It is close to many attracttions and has good rooms, services and excellent staff.I would most definitely stay here again next time visiting Amsterdam

<Author>Harrald
<Content>Call before you book We stayed in the Amsterdam Marriott for 4 days in early Dec. We had 2 rooms on the third floor that were down the hall from each other. Most nights both rooms were awakened by the sounds of construction during the night. One room had a flood in the bathroom from the room above that was fixed quickly. One morning the elevators didn't work for about 30ish minutes. To be fair to the hotel they are in the middle of renovation. I have stayed in Marriott properties for many years and in many countries. This was by far the worst one I've ever stayed in. As I stated though, they are renovating. If you plan on using this hotel I suggest you call ahead and see if they have finished the work. Also if you need to stay there soon, you should ask for a new room.If I return to Amsterdam I will choose another location and check on the status of the Marriott while in the city. The location is good and the tram stops outside the door. The hotel restaurant is overpriced (like all hotel resaurants) but there are a number of other choices within a few minutes walk. I took no pictures since it would be unfair to the hotel to show rooms that will soon be updated.

<Author>FingalDublin
<Content>first rate Myself and my wife stayed for 2 nights in the Marriott in late august and found it to be excellent. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Rooms Overall, I would have given this hotel an excellent rating had the dining options been better. The room we stayed in was very nice, very spacious, and a had a wonderful view out onto the street. We had two queen beds and both worked well with the room. This room was definitely not one of your typical small European rooms. My only large complaint about the property was the dining. The first night, because of jet lag, I ate in the hotel bar. The food wasn't bad, but the service was slow. The other dining options, their fine dining, didn't look to be too fine, so we opted out of eating there and instead ate across the street at Bice which was very good. There is also a Pizza Hut which occupies the hotel building which devalues one's perception of the dining that the hotel offers. I'm in the hotel business and putting a pizza hut in a four star hotel would be something I would avoid at all costs.The service was good as the concierge was very helpful for dinner and for sight seeing. The only small complaint was how long it took to have certain things delivered to the room. I had a power converter delivered to the room and that took what seemed like 20 minutes.Overall, the hotel itself is very nice and the lobby is nicely done. My only complaint is the dining.

<Author>RWAppleWannabe
<Content>Great location, extremely comfy beds I stayed at this Marriott over Memorial Day weekend 2006. Using Priceline, my husband and I (and friends we traveled with) got great deals on our rooms - we couldn't have been happier with the location! It was just a 5 to 10-minute walk to Vondelpark, Rijksmuseum, Van Gogh Museum, and great concert venues like the Melk Wag. Although the Leidseplein (the large square on which the hotel sits) is well-served by trams, we much preferred walking everywhere, which was easy thanks to the hotel's location. It took just 20 minutes along the very scenic and nearby Prinsengracht to reach the Anne Frank House and to take in the stores and cafes in the Jordaan neighborhood. After long days of touring and late nights enjoying the nightlife, we particularly appreciated the superior beds. The mattress has a featherbed top, and the down comforters and super-fluffly pillows reminded me of the beds at the Ritz Carlton. I was surprised and impressed. The concierge was always helpful and friendly when I asked for directions to different places. Overall, the Marriott's a great choice if you're in town for a few days playing tourist.PS - the majority of the Rijksmuseum is closed for renovation right now, so check on what's open before you buy the pricey tickets there. When we went, just a fraction of the rooms were open and masterpieces were jumbled together in small rooms. We had a much better time at the Van Gogh museum than at the Rijksmuseum.

<Author>LauraKK
<Content>Convient  We were unexpectedly pleased with the Amsterdam Marriot during our recent 5 day stay there. It was ''tulip season'', and all the cute little canal BB's were booked, so we grabbed what we could get and took the Marriot. We were afraid it would be an American ''tour bus'' experience, but were so surprised with how nice it was. First of all, the location is terrific. You are 3 minutes away from the major restaurant areas., bus to the airport ($2.50 USD, what a bargain), and several of the canal cruises and the Rembrandt and Van Gough museums. Location could NOT have been any better.The rooms were very large by European standards, and the showers powerful and linens very nice and comfy. The staff was friendly, helpful and knowledgeable about sights in Amsterdam. Despite the large numbers of American tourists, there was always someone at the Concierge waiting for us, and willing to go out of their way to help us with postage for postcards, booking restaurants, getting theatre or museum tickets, etc. The location was perfect, as mentioned. You are within easy walking distance of all the major sites and restaurants, museums. We had a lovely balcony view of the canal, and couldn't have been happier. We'll definitely stay here next time.BTW, breakfast in nice, but way too expensive for Amsterdam. Book without breakfast and explore the area within 3 blocks of hotel for fabulous breadfast fare for 1/5 the cost!

<Author>view2
<Content>Good hotel We stayed at the Amsterdam Marriott during Queensday weekend. Arriving noon Friday there was a long check in / out que. We later learnt this was due to problems with the newly installed computer system, hence express (in-room via TV) check-out was not working and everyone had to queue up in the lobby.First impressions good (despite the queue), staff were welcoming us and smiling. On our previous Amsterdam trips we have had some terrible hotel experiences (i.e. Old Quarter), so we have learned the hard way that AMS hotel rooms are small. The rooms in Marriott were decent sized, though small compared to any US Marriott. Still, nicely appointed and clean. 28 TV, mini bar, wines offered for 7 Euro, which is not bad. Decent amenities in bathroom. Large safe. Ice-machine down the corridor, which suited our party weekend (Queensday) nicely.Nightly turn-down service, which basically is making the bed ready for night and leaving a little chocolate for each guest. Used the business center on Saturday morning, my girlfirend and I each got a 45 min Internet access to the computers in the business center. This set ut back 15 Euros each. Unbelievably pricey. In fact most extras were highly priced. We booked through Priceline, thus had no breakfast included. Because it cost 26 Euros each we never ate breakfast at the hotel. Just not worth it for breakfast. Our rate was 108 Euros a night, which I think is a good rate for this hotel standard in Amsterdam. They mentioned Priceline at check-in and that it was pre-paid. No problem.Location is excellent, right in Leidseplein and close to museums. Much nicer area to stay in that Dam Square / Damrak or the Red Light District which we have stayed in previously.Recommended.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good staff let down by terrible admin facilities I have stayed at the Amsterdam Marriott on a number of occasions and had pretty hassle-free stays. This time however was not as good. First the positives, the staff are extremely welcoming and friendly, even more so if you speak Dutch as I do. I was made very much to feel at home. The rooms are a good size for Amsterdam and the hotel is in the heart of the action, a few metres walk from Leidseplein. Coming from Schiphol, the train to Centraal Station is fine, however the tram ride to Leidseplein can take a while as they stop for ever to let passengers on. The rooms were also very clean. However, they have just installed a new computer system which had more than its fair share of problems. First of all, check in was delayed, with many guests hanging around in the lobby, by the fact that there had been a computer failure. I handed over my credit card as a guarantee, however, 10 days later they haven't taken the authorization off my account and more than that, they have taken even more money off it. When I called up to find out what had happened, they had absolutely no idea and could not help me at all. All they could do was apologize and tell me that my data are completely secure and that the authorizations should disappear soon. Not much comfort to me. I have been advised by my credit card company to wait for a few more days and then to take more action if necessary. I would recommend perhaps leaving a cash deposit instead while they sort out their technology. The other thing is the in-room wireless broadband, why is something that should be free to business travellers, extortionately priced at EUR20 per day?
