<Author>kjh888
<Content>Accommodation good, service disappointing We stayed at the Marriott Amsterdam for Easter weekend 2006. Overall, it provided a high standard of accomodation, however service was disappointing and I at 鈧?15 a night I wouldn't say it was great value for money.The location of the hotel is great - at the southern end of the Liedelsplein and very close to the Vondelpark. Trams 1,2 and 5 run regularly from the central station and you can pick up a canal tour from very close by.Perhaps it was because we arrived on Good Friday, but the check-in queue was long and slow moving. Our room request of a high floor room and a cot were met however. The room was quite small but spotlessly clean and had most of the expected facilities. We were disappointed at no tea and coffee facilities in the room. The bathroom was dated, but clean - I would expect more from a 5 star hotel however. Our room was supposedly executive - I'm not sure what made it qualify for this rating!Breakfast was included in our room rate but costs between 22 and 27 Euros if you purchase separately. We had free and unlimited choice from the buffet which was vast and good quality - masses of choice and even Stollen and easter eggs on Easter Sunday. There were plenty of tables, although we always had to queue to be seated. Staff were helpful and friendly. On our final day they provided breakfast to take away as we had an early flight - this was very convenient.We travelled with a toddler and the hotel catered for this well- a cot was provided in the room and a highchair for breakfast. Staff were considerate towards the need of a small child too.Service on the whole was disappointing for a 5 star hotel - our room only came with one bathrobe, and we asked for another one at reception three times (we stayed three nights, and asked every night). They never delivered and we ended up stopping a passing maid for assistance. It was such a simple request and yet they failed to meet it 3 times! It wasn't important to our stay, but it was the principle.I wouldn't discourage people from staying at this hotel, but feel it is more 4 star than 5 star, and might not be the best example of the Marriott brand.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, $110 on Priceline Hotel is one block from the tram station (convenient for luggage) and a 20 minute stroll through interesting neighborhoods from Centraal Train Station. When we arrive around 9:30 am we were told that they were cleaning a very nice room for us. It couldn't have been better-on the fourth floor-directly facing the intersection. We had fun watching the trams, pedestrians and bikers and the more distant view of Liedersplein with its cafes and nighttime performers. The room was totally soundproofed so there was no noice despite the hubub outside. When I have bid on priceline before and contacted the hotel to ask for a room with a non smoking room with two beds, I have invariably been told that my request would be noted but that there was no guarantee with priceline. In this instance, the hotel promptly emailed me that they would be happy to meet my request. Front desk and concierge staff were very friendly and helpful. Two canalboats departed from across the street, there is a pancake house also in the square across the street, a tourist information office, shopping, cafes, bakeries etc. one block away.

<Author>lass=
<Content>For $100/night on Priceline, man what a deal... Our low nightly rate probably colored our view of this place, but at $100 a night I think its a great value.First, the location: the Marriot is between the Leidesplein and Vondelpark, which is really a great area. The Liedesplein is the party center of Amsterdam, and is chock full of restaurants, bars, coffeeshops and other people partying. Vondelpark/Museumplein, as the name implies, contains a nice park and some world class museums.Second, the property is really deluxe. It has uniformed doormen, bellman and concierge. There are two eateries, a bar, a gift shop and a gratis morning coffee concession in the lobby. There is a free laundry on the second floor. Okay, so from the outside it does resemble the Politburo Marriot - but I didn't care how it looked on the outside.Third, the rooms are nice for Europe. That is, our room had a safe, ironing board, iron, unbelievably comfortable king sized bed and a small television. As is mentioned in other reviews, the heating and cooling leaves something to be desired, but by opening and closing the window, we were able to stay comfortable. The bath is large and the shower is great.The concierge staff was extremely helpful. This old dude gave me directions to the Dampkring Coffee Shop without batting an eye. Hell he plotted it out on a map. Another of the concierge staff gave us the heads up on beating the line at the Van Gogh Museum by selling us our tickets (at the same price as the museum). We strolled past the other art fans and were checking out the Potato Eaters in no time at at all.Getting there was easy from Schiphol Airport. We hopped a $5 train from the airport to Centraal Station. We then hopped on a tram (lines 1, 2 or 5) and were at the Marriot ten minutes later. When you get on the tram, tell the conducter that you need to get off at the Marriot and he or she will tell you when to get off over the PA.Transportation around Amsterdam is easy from the Marriot. Three different tram lines run from Central Station by the hotel all day. We explored the whole city by jumping on and off trams.We found the Dutch to be the coolest people on earth. They speak English better than I do, they are very friendly and are perhaps the best looking people on the face of the earth. We cannot wait to go back.If I had to pay more than $100, I would be far less enthusiastic. But for the price we paid, it was the best deal in town.  
<Date>May 7, 2005

<Author>SWAMPRAT
<Content>Great location You can't beat the location of the Amsterdam Marriott. There are bars, restaurants and coffee shops everywhere within walking distance. It's also within walking distance to the main museums (Van Gogh, Riks Museum, etc.). The best restaurant we ate at was Puri Mas (ristafjel - typical Indonesian rice table meal). The food was excellent, plentiful and the staff were friendly and accommodating. The only problem we had was with the A/C in our room. If you are concerned about being able to control the climate in your room, make sure you ask if the A/C or heating is individually controlled when you make the reservation. I found out that in these older hotels in Europe, even if there is a thermostat in your room, that doesn't mean that you can really control the temperature. It's pretty much on winter (heating) or summer (cooling) overall, and controlled from a central location. Fortunately, we were able to keep our room cool by opening the window.Other than that, the rooms were clean, beds were comfortable (double beds instead of twins is a plus) and the location is excellent. I'd definitely stay here again.  
<Date>May 3, 2005

<Author>ooookch
<Content>Pro's and Con's, and too expensive. I spent a weekend in February with my girlfriend in the Amsterdam Marriott. The location is great, close to Leidseplein area with its restaurants, bars, cinemas and theaters and also close to the museums. The staff was very nice and helpful, check in took quite a while though. The A/C is very loud. Tiny bathroom which definitely needs an overhaul as it shows traces of many years of usage. So the room is not up to Marriott standards, however the prices are. Wouldn't go there again; I usually prefer Marriotts over Intercontis, but in Amsterdam it is definitely vice versa.

<Author>PhilInSuffolk
<Content>Excellent location, generally good but some problems Stayed here in February for a conference. The location is excellent - handy for the restaurants towards the centre as well as the Van Gogh and Rembrandt museums. Getting there from the airport without using taxis is easy, too - train to the Central Station and then trams 1, 5 or 6 - total cost 5 euro. Note - it's best to have some Euro coins to buy tickets from the automatic machines.Most of the stay was good - the room was a good size and the facilities were in good order. On the plus side, the windows opened, there was broadband internet access (and I was only charged a day, despite using it for 3 days), the bed was comfortable and the bath was good. However:I asked for non-feather bedding. The pillows were replaced quickly, but the duvet was just taken off and not replaced, despite my asking for a non-feather one on a separate occasion.Internet access is expensive - 29.95 euroI was charged for bar expenditure I didn't make (which was refunded)Breakfast is (as seems often to be the case) very expensive - 18 euro minimum - make sure it's included.The air-com makes a noise like a jumbo taking off, and mine seemed only to heat with no control.They have a security system that means you have to use your room key to activate the lift - this is acceptable for going up from ground, but coming down?I hated the smell they pipe into the corridors.On balance I'd use it again, but they should tackle the niggles.

<Author>TaraR
<Content>Great place to stay! Three of us stayed at the Amsterdam Marriott for a long weekend at the end of Oct 2004. Room was equivalent to what I have would expect in a US hotel and much bigger than any other Eurpean hotel room I have stayed in. I requested 2 double bed and all of us agreed that they were VERY comfortable (featherbed and great pillows). Location was great and was an easy train  tram ride from the airport. I was hoping to find something a little cheaper than 178 Euros / night - but this actually was one of the lower rates I could find (I looked at both triple rooms and 2 seperate rooms). After reading other reviews, I tried priceline a couple of times for 2 rooms at btwn $77 - $99 - but no offers were accepted. We did not eat breakfast at the hotel or eat at any of the restaurants or use room service. Fitness center was very nice (for a hotel) - 2 treadmills, 4 bikes, 2 EFXs and lots of weights. I used it everyday we were there. Overall, I would definitely recommend!!

<Author>Dolly123
<Content>Wonderful Stay! In December 2003, I had 3 days to kill between business trips (one week in Poland, then 4 days in The Hague); flying home to the US and then back to Europe was out of the question ... so I decided to cool my heels in Amsterdam. I'd visited Amsterdam several times before, and with the rush to get all my Christmas activities done before the 2 weeks of business travel, I really just wanted somewhere to veg-out ... and the Amsterdam Marriott was the PERFECT choice. I treated myself to an Executive Room, something I've never done in all my travels. Check-in was a breeze - quick, efficient and friendly. The Conseirge answered every question/request with accuracy and a smile. The room was huge (could have held a roller derby in there). The king bed was the most comfortable hotel bed I have EVER slept in. The Executive Club Room (access came with the rate) was quiet, classy and spotlessly clean; breakfast here was very nice (typical continental plus smoked salmon, fresh fruit and few other extras); my favorite ECR amenity was the available-24-hours-a-day Cappuccino machine (sorry Marriott, you lost money on this guest). I even hung out here a few hours each afternoon working on my laptop - got lots done with all the quiet and endless supply of coffees, teas, and sweet and savory munchies. The fitness center was well-equiped: 4 treadmills, 4 bicycles, rowing machines, nautilus equipment and free weights; TVs in every corner so you could catch up on news, sports, and make the work-out time fly by. I basically locked myself in my room for 3 days, only going to the ECR, the fitness center and the occassional walk outside (freezing in Dec). Since it was too cold to venture outside after dark and I was alone, I took a risk on Room Service: Fabulous! The Cream Tomato Soup is to die for (and I am a serious Food Snob), as is the Caesar Salad. I ordered several other times over my 3-day stay, and all were exceptional. My only complaint: HAVE THE MASSAGE/SPA STAFF AVAILABLE 7 DAYS A WEEK!!! With the state I was in, I would have booked a massage, pedicure, facial, etc - but the spa facilities weren't available on Sat afternoon, Sunday or Monday. I left the Marriott, as my husband would say, fat, dumb and happy! Highly, highly recommended.
